  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a9a556cc-0772-4c60-84b1-64ac923889f9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText2191129832701576918" style="display:none"><b>The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling series that inspired the international hit video game: <i>The Witcher.</i></b><br />For over a century, humans, dwarves, gnomes, and elves have lived together in relative peace. But times have changed, the uneasy peace is over, and now the races are fighting once again. The only good elf, it seems, is a dead elf.<br /><br />Geralt of Rivia, the cunning assassin known as The Witcher, has been waiting for the birth of a prophesied child. This child has the power to change the world - for good, or for evil.<br /><br />As the threat of war hangs over the land and the child is hunted for her extraordinary powers, it will become Geralt's responsibility to protect them all - and the Witcher never accepts defeat.<br /><br />The Witcher returns in this sequel to <em>The Last Wish</em>, as the inhabitants of his world become embroiled in a state of total war.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_68458').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_68458').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_68458').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/344608-i-was-thinking-about-reading-the-witcher">I was thinking about reading The Witcher books in anticipation of The Witcher 3 video game.

Having no prior knowledge of The Witcher universe, I wondered if anyone could tell me the relationship between the books and the games - Are they direct adaptions, borrow elements, or just the same characters in the same universe with no other links?

Thanks!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_344608'><a id="like_count_community_question_344608" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/344608?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6043781-blood-of-elves">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/344608-i-was-thinking-about-reading-the-witcher">5 years ago</a>
</li>

</li>
</ul>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7253517"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1407156508i/7253517.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7253517">Μιχάλης</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The games are a loose sequel to the books, meaning that they come after the seventh novel and borrow on a lot of events from the books (from instance,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The games are a loose sequel to the books, meaning that they come after the seventh novel and borrow on a lot of events from the books (from instance, the Strigga storyline from the Last Wish comes up in The Witcher Game) but, at the same time, they are not a strict sequel as some secondary characters are reinterpreted(is The Professor)<br /><br />At the same time, the characterisation of the characters is non-consistent, having even the main character being much different in books and in the game.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1944617707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1944617707" />
    <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis"><img alt="Joey Woolfardis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490696206p2/4639825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1944617707?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey Woolfardis" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis">Joey Woolfardis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575084841" href="/book/show/6321854-blood-of-elves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=intriguing-but-ultimately-naff">intriguing-but-ultimately-naff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=masculine">masculine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=myths-magic-and-mordor">myths-magic-and-mordor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ce20">ce20</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=polish">polish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944617707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18040515125971973603"><i>This review can be found on <a href='http://amaranthinereads.blogspot.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amaranthine Reads</a></i>.<br/><br/>Considering how well-written and quick-paced the short story prequel collection <i>The Last Wish</i> by Andrzej Sapkowski was, this was ridiculously disappointing and underwhelming. We have the same characters as was to be found in <i>The Last Wish</i>, and we had their personalities expanded and explored further, but we had none of the excitement or fantasy that was found there.<br/><br/><i>Blood of Elves</i> is very slow and very closed-off. We spend far too much time in one pla</span>
  <span id="freeText18040515125971973603" style="display:none"><i>This review can be found on <a href="http://amaranthinereads.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amaranthine Reads</a></i>.<br /><br />Considering how well-written and quick-paced the short story prequel collection <i>The Last Wish</i> by Andrzej Sapkowski was, this was ridiculously disappointing and underwhelming. We have the same characters as was to be found in <i>The Last Wish</i>, and we had their personalities expanded and explored further, but we had none of the excitement or fantasy that was found there.<br /><br /><i>Blood of Elves</i> is very slow and very closed-off. We spend far too much time in one place alone, and we follow conversations at a snail's pace to the point where what they're saying is no longer important but pointless chit-chat. It takes over half the book for us to leave Geralt and Ciri, who have taken up most of the book doing pretty much nothing in one place. The narrator is supposed to be omniscient, but it feels more like first-person narrative with just one or two dips elsewhere to move the rather vague plot along.<br /><br />It's such a huge disappointment because the inclusion of our own folklore and fairytales in <i>The Last Wish</i> was a very good idea and following Geralt as he went about the countryside tackling monsters and demons (which is the job of the Witcher) was exciting, refreshing and kept the stories moving along. In <i>Blood of Elves</i> we meet one monster and little else.<br /><br />It is mostly full of political intrigue, none of which is that interesting, nor does it deviate from the generic fantasy trope of races warring with races, crossing borders and sacking cities. But even then, with the generic fantasy tropes, we barely even get in to them because the characters are too busy having inane conversations whilst, presumably, just standing about being targets.<br /><br />There was, however, a better set of female characters in this, though it was a bit too James Bond-esque how they all seemingly dropped their knickers are the mere sight of Geralt of Rivia. If one can get past this obvious High Fantasy trope and author-projection, we see some female characters that are developed beyond their breasts, but only just.<br /><br />It's a relatively fun fantasy day-out. A quick read, won't challenge you much and will give you a good dose of non-YA fantasy goodness if that's what you're looking for (it's why I gravitated toward it) but it is by no means anything brilliant or ground-breaking. I will, however, finish the series, maybe pick up the other short story collection I haven't gotten around to <b>and</b> possibly play the game that was inspired by it.<br /><br />(It's worth pointing out that this book is the first of a series, despite GoodReads naming it the third. This book is the first full-length novel and makes up the series of full length books, with two anthologies of short stories taking up 1st and 2nd in the series.)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/infiniteANDdarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/infinitedarlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://uk.pinterest.com/infinitedarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Shop</a> | <a href="https://www.etsy.com/uk/shop/infiniteANDdarling" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_2568338996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568338996" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568338996?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568338996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1073069304203425147">Blood of Elves is chronologically the 3rd entry within The Witcher saga. Whereas previously all the short stories followed Geralt of Rivia working on certain monster assassination assignments, within Blood of Elves he is one of 3 or 4 main characters that we share the minds of. For the novels, you can start here but I wouldn't recommend it. I found that I completely loved the groundwork I'd put in with the previous narratives and then hearing about the past stories mentioned of which I'd already</span>
  <span id="freeText1073069304203425147" style="display:none">Blood of Elves is chronologically the 3rd entry within The Witcher saga. Whereas previously all the short stories followed Geralt of Rivia working on certain monster assassination assignments, within Blood of Elves he is one of 3 or 4 main characters that we share the minds of. For the novels, you can start here but I wouldn't recommend it. I found that I completely loved the groundwork I'd put in with the previous narratives and then hearing about the past stories mentioned of which I'd already read such as recollecting thought regarding meeting the Golden Dragon and about the macabre events that happened at the downfall of Cintra. It was also an excellent feeling meeting familiar characters (often a bit too spontaneously) that we'd briefly crossed paths with within the previous books. I can't state it enough that this book is so much deeper and more enjoyable if you've read what comes beforehand. The important side characters from the recent stories are more prominent here, most notably Ciri and Yennefer. I'm gutted we don't see more of one of my favourite characters, the womanising troubadour Dandelion. <br /><br />The tale starts at a safe haven underneath a giant tree where Dandelion and his apprentice tell the epic poem of Geralt. We know the stories if we've read the previous entries but the poetry and the action is accentuated for the audience and is more picturesque, beautiful, and heightened in this form. Dandelion is the finest bard in the land who causes the ladies to swoon, the lords to be jealous and the brothel owners to panic! The ensemble of all assembled then discuss what happened at the end of the depicted action. Was Geralt murdered? Did the Child of Destiny, the Princess Ciri escape? Did her and Geralt meet up as was prophecised? It's a really intriguing beginning and sets the action up expertly. Geralt is an extremely famous Witcher whose name is world-renowned. Everyone claims to know him and his exploits but he's not been witnessed in two years so how much is a mere fabrication to attract the attention of revelers in a bar on a weekend evening? <br /><br />In this outing, Ciri, the child of Destiny is essentially the main character with Geralt being more of a shadowy father figure who aids her development as an upcoming Witcher although she also has magical capabilities she does not understand. He is the infamous Witcher, Yennefer is an enchantress and "will they-won't they" love interest and although not the biological child of the aforementioned she seems like a perfect mix of arguably the other two main characters. <br /><br />This tale was much deeper than what had come beforehand and as I've previously mentioned I wish to read all of these before the Netflix series is released. The first 30% is mainly focused on Ciri's training at the Witcher halls of Kaer Morten under the watchful gaze of the remaining handful of Witchers but also sorceresses Triss and Yennefer who are both former love interests of Geralt. Geralt does love Ciri as a father would and their relationship is complex, loving in a lack-0f-emotion way from Geralt's perspective. He's a complex character as he's been genetically mutated to be a heartless monster killer but he has extreme morals and will not take sides in any sort of debacle. One persons' right is another ones' wrong and he shouldn't take sides and that's not what he has been manipulated for.<br /><br />Honestly, there isn't too much action throughout this novel, but that's fine. This is the foundation of what will no doubt be an exceptional next five books. The main drama is caused by a fire-scarred magical-wielding individual who has an unknown vendetta against Geralt and wants Ciri. Imagine if the Queen on a chessboard was infinitely more valuable and in the eyes of the soon to be warring nations this (even though they don't know if she's alive) 12-year-old young lady has a very important part to play. Child of Destiny isn't a title that everyone is able to flaunt after all. <br /><br />Blood of Elves is very conversation heavy. Sometimes, with players having similar and confusing names it does get a bit over-bearing. Often a conversation will have eight contributors but it doesn't always make it obvious who is saying what so in these scenes I found my mind bouncing around thinking... "who said that?" - "who was that to?" etc? The vibe and the point of the scene are expressed well but it's not always easy to keep a perfect picture of progression. <br /><br />I loved the majority of the short stories and only a few remain weak and uninteresting in my mind. This seemed like a well constructed but quite safe progression to the novel side of things. It didn't really have an exciting finale. The only event that could be considered as such was a confrontation at the eighty percent mark and then we were gifted a Ciri training session to conclude. This series isn't perfect yet. However, I am really enjoying following this interesting and multi-layered cast. This could go on to being one of my favourite fantasy series. At this point I believe I've only witnessed the tip of the iceberg and Ciri's destiny and the Witcher's influence is amazingly intriguing. I can't wait to read the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1073069304203425147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3111382369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3111382369" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3111382369?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_1773915985" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773915985" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773915985?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773915985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1935775799711196949">This book signifies a sharp departure from the previous two. The first and second ones were collections of short stories mostly told from Geralt the Witcher POV. This time this is a full-length novel with multiple POVs. Actually we only see Geralt's POV in just one chapter - and a shortish one too. In my opinion the book still shows its origins in short story format as the transitions between the chapters are mostly not continuous. Instead they start with a jump in time to give a flashback to co</span>
  <span id="freeText1935775799711196949" style="display:none">This book signifies a sharp departure from the previous two. The first and second ones were collections of short stories mostly told from Geralt the Witcher POV. This time this is a full-length novel with multiple POVs. Actually we only see Geralt's POV in just one chapter - and a shortish one too. In my opinion the book still shows its origins in short story format as the transitions between the chapters are mostly not continuous. Instead they start with a jump in time to give a flashback to connect the events between the previous chapter and current time. <br><br>As to the plot it is quite easy to outline. The last story of the second book left Geralt stuck with - supposedly - his destiny; namely a child (not his). The poor Witcher was doing all he could and even more to prove that destiny does not exists - at least in his case, only to fail spectacularly. Coming back to destiny's child:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476286452i/20823254._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="385" alt="Destiny's Child" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>oops sorry, wrong picture. It turns out everybody and their brother want to find the poor kid. I mean it literally: it was easier to count the number of named characters of the novel who could not care less about Geralt's protégé than the searchers. I also need to mention some of them were so insistent they would not hesitate to leave a dead body (or ten) if somebody happened to be in their way. Now Geralt needs to provide the protection. He also wants to remain neutral in the intensifying political games and this task turns out to be practically impossible unlike disposing of hired thugs. <br><br>I have some complaints about the book. Geralt is supposed to be a monster hunter first and foremost. Well he hunted exactly one monster in here; none others bothered even to show up. There is something to be said about the evil created by humans being the biggest monster of them all, but I seriously missed a tentacled multi-headed poison-tailed chitin-armored creature waiting for its butt to be kicked by a skilled professional. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476287882i/20823429._SY540_.jpg" width="405" height="550" alt="Chtulhu" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that I finished the book, I cast my mind back and realize that not much actually happened here: a lot of talks, a lot of politics, but by the end most of the characters remained right where they started. Things were brewing, but had not come to boiling point yet. <br><br>For all the slowness the book has charm. I cannot quite put my finger on it, but somehow I was never bored reading and the read itself was quite fast. For this reason I give the higher rating than I usually do for such book: 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1935775799711196949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6415386-blood-of-elves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1878979579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9116601821430867628"><b>Geralt of The Last Wish, where art thou</b>?!<br/><br/><b>Do I need</b> to call the puny human authorities and tell them to issue an AMBER alert? Have the obnoxious aliens <b>abducted you</b> again, as I suspect they did in book 2? Or is it that the Evil Russians™ are <b>holding you hostage</b> until I surrender my East Siberian Sea dominion? That very well could be. The <b>Fluffy Siberian Bunnies</b> (FSB™) can get bloody shrimping devious like that sometimes. Then again, I don't think that this is what happened here. You know what I t</span>
  <span id="freeText9116601821430867628" style="display:none"><b>Geralt of The Last Wish, where art thou</b>?!<br><br><b>Do I need</b> to call the puny human authorities and tell them to issue an AMBER alert? Have the obnoxious aliens <b>abducted you</b> again, as I suspect they did in book 2? Or is it that the Evil Russians™ are <b>holding you hostage</b> until I surrender my East Siberian Sea dominion? That very well could be. The <b>Fluffy Siberian Bunnies</b> (FSB™) can get bloody shrimping devious like that sometimes. Then again, I don't think that this is what happened here. You know what I think, my Little Barnacles? <b>I think Geralt decided to bolt</b>. Why, you ask? Seems pretty obvious to me: the previous instalment <b>nearly did him in</b>. First things first, the guy's <b>Monster Slaying Quota</b> (MSQ™) dropped dramatically. Second things second, he was viciously attacked by brutal waves of <b>utter boredom and blah blah blah</b>. And third things third, he had to endure some major <b>Lovey Dovey Drama Crap</b> (LDDC™). I'm telling you, my Lovely Arthropods I would have pulled the <b>Now You See Me Now You Don't Stint</b> (NYSMNYDS™) too, had I been in his place.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518109134ra/25026369.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, that is indeed my little self very discretely pulling a NYSMNYDS™.</i><br><br><b>Okay</b>, I know what you Annoying Decapods are going to tell me: "but, <s>gloriously nefarious</s> Sarah <s>we are in such awe of</s>, Geralt hasn't gone anywhere! <b>Geralt is right here</b>! <b>In this book</b>!" Naïve, naïve, Little Barnacles. I'm afraid you've been had like a bunch of provincial krill. It's not Geralt we're dealing with in this instalment! It's <b>gErAlT, his duplicitous, evilly evil twin</b>! You have no idea how shrewd and calculating the guy is. And bloody shrimping <b>presumptuous</b>, too! He actually had the nerve to come up with his very own <b>precepts</b> for this book! Don't believe me? <b>Check this out</b>:<br><br><u>
  <b>The Outrageously Outrageous Witcher Commandments According to <s>Garp</s> gErAlT (OOWCAt<s>G</s>G™)</b>
</u>:<br><br>☠ <b>Violently butcher monsters you shall refrain from</b>.<br><b>Yes</b>, this is kinda sorta awkward when supernatural beast slaying is kinda sorta <b>your calling and day job</b>. But what's a guy to do to get <b>PETA</b> off his back? See the tiny predicament here? The only solution is obviously for you to do the <b>Pest Control Thing</b> (PCT™) once <s>in a while</s> per book tops, so that your street cred doesn't get <b>thoroughly ruined</b> and stuff. Your life will no longer have a <b>meaning</b>, but that really is quite an <b>insignificant price to pay</b> in the grand scheme of things, is it not?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518111453ra/25026541.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>See, the Libidinously Mustached Duo (LMD™) doesn't think it's a big deal, either.</i><br><br>☠ <b>Only a few pages told from your POV your <s>slightly hysterical</s> fans you shall provide with</b>.<br>Because you are of the erroneously wrong opinion that <b>absence makes the black, withered heart grow fonder</b> and stuff. Well, some <b>People of the Forever Right Opinion</b> (PofFRO™) happen to think <b>absence makes the pincers get sharper</b>. But hey, to each their own <b>and all that fish</b>.<br><br>☠ <b>Much needless blah blah blah crap let your fellow cast members gleefully indulge in you shall</b>.<br>In the meantime a <b>well-deserved nap</b> most joyfully you will enjoy (while thinking "muahahahaha and stuff" to your smug little self). <s>Bored</s> <b>Slightly uninterested readers</b> be damned and all that. If they can't appreciate <b>coma-inducing goodness</b> kindly brought to them by a bunch of queens/kings/rulers/whatever, it's their problem, not yours. <b>Besides</b>, if they think this book is the cure to insomnia, they should try and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127455.The_Lies_of_Locke_Lamora__Gentleman_Bastard___1_" title="The Lies of Locke Lamora (Gentleman Bastard, #1) by Scott Lynch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lies of Locke Lamora</a>. If they're lucky they'll only end up with an <b>acute case of narcolepsy</b>. So QED and stuff. It's time for a little <b>Smug gErAlT Muahahahaha-ing</b> (SGM™) again.<br><br>☠ <b>Deceitfully bring in a disgustingly kidnap-worthy little kid to sneakily soften the tougher shrimps out there you shall</b>:<br>Make her all sorts of <b>revoltingly cute</b> with huge <b>ass-kicking potential</b> and wondrous <b>smartass</b> abilities to weaken your intended victim's reinforced, titanium-coated exoskeleton. <b>Cunningly hint</b> at the possibility that said brat might one day be a <b>greater character</b> than your little self. This is far from the truth, of course. No one is, or ever will be, greater than your <b>astonishingly fabulous (and yet so humble) little self</b>. This is naught but a diabolically Machiavellian scheme to make sure some crustaceans will continue reading <s>Ciri's</s> your most fascinating adventures. <b>Hook, line and sinker</b>, the bloody shrimping shrimps are bloody shrimping done for. <b>Mission accomplished and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518112394ra/25026635.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Told you gErAlT was nothing like Geralt. Ha.</i><br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>What the Fishing Fish is Fishing Going On with this Series I Demand Both and Explanation and a Formal Apology Crappy Non Review</b> (WtFFiFGOwtSIDBaEaaFACNR™) is: dear Mr Sapkowski, give Geralt back <b>NOW</b>. And I don't mean gErAlT, <b>I mean bloody shrimping Geralt</b>. As in my <b>super hot sexey badass monster slaying boyfriend</b> from The Last Wish. Puny humans might get hurt somewhat <b>painfully</b> (and also suffer a slightly <b>excruciating</b> fate, by the way) if you don't comply. <b>But hey, no pressure and stuff</b>.<br><br>· <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815326876" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a> ★★★★★<br>· <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878979060" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a> ★★★<br>· <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878980031" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time of Contempt</a> ★★<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>Geralt, Geralt, Geralt</b>...What to do with you? I hope you do realize that I've only ever kicked one boyfriend out of my <b>High Security Harem</b> before. Surely you do not want to suffer the same fate? Especially since the boyfriend in question was <b>Wimpish Happy Dresden</b> (WHD™) *shudders* Pretty sure you'd hate to receive the same treatment as this <b>substandard puny human</b>, huh? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511117955ra/24484226.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Yep</b>, that's what I thought. Well you know what? If you want to stay <b>safely locked up</b> in the Harem, you're going to have to work for it. I'm giving you one last bloody shrimping chance, so <b>don't screw things up</b> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14781491.The_Time_of_Contempt__The_Witcher___2_" title="The Time of Contempt (The Witcher, #2) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Time of Contempt</a>, or else...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517849144i/25007639.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ Full <b>Not Even A Full Chapter Written From Geralt's POV This is Outrageous This is Unacceptable This Cannot Be This Will Not Do We are Not Amused Crustaceans at the Ready and Stuff Crappy Non Review</b> (NEAFCWFGPOVTiOTiUTCBTWNDWaNACatRaSCNR™) to come. <br><br><b>P.S.</b> Geralt dear, butchering monsters is always a plus. Think about that for a minute or two, will you?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9116601821430867628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_793290591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793290591" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793290591?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=lovely-ladies">lovely-ladies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2010-2012">2010-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=extraordinary-gentlemen">extraordinary-gentlemen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=the-white-wolf">the-white-wolf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793290591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14773911870744341687"><b>
  <i>"The era of the sword and axe is nigh, the era of the wolf’s blizzard. The Time of the White Chill and the White Light is nigh, the Time of Madness and the Time of Contempt: Tedd Deireádh, the Time of End. The world will die amidst frost and be reborn with the new sun. It will be reborn of the Elder Blood, of Hen Ichaer, of the seed that has been sown. A seed which will not sprout but will burst into flame. Ess’tuath esse! Thus it shall be! Watch for the signs! What signs these shall be, I sa</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14773911870744341687" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"The era of the sword and axe is nigh, the era of the wolf’s blizzard. The Time of the White Chill and the White Light is nigh, the Time of Madness and the Time of Contempt: Tedd Deireádh, the Time of End. The world will die amidst frost and be reborn with the new sun. It will be reborn of the Elder Blood, of Hen Ichaer, of the seed that has been sown. A seed which will not sprout but will burst into flame. Ess’tuath esse! Thus it shall be! Watch for the signs! What signs these shall be, I say unto you: first the earth will flow with the blood of Aen Seidhe, the Blood of Elves..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Cintra is burning.<br /><br />The legions of the Nilfgaardian Empire have crossed the Yaruga again, and the independent future of the Northern Kingdoms is in grave peril. It is against this backdrop that the story opens. The story of Cirilla, Ciri, the orphaned princess with a mysterious destiny. Of the great struggle between the free kingdoms of the north and their overwhelming imperial adversary. And of the lone mutated witcher known as Gwynbleidd, the White Wolf.<br /><br />And so it begins.<br /><br />After introducing Geralt of Rivia, the White Wolf himself, in a set of stunning short stories, Sapkowski kicks the main story off with a bang as <i>Blood of Elves</i> introduces a somewhat different, yet astounding, fantasy epic.<br /><br />I first read <i>Blood of Elves</i> many years ago now, after having played the first game and read the absodamnlutely amazing short story collection <i>The Last Wish</i>. While I would seriously consider that book a masterpiece of the fantasy genre, this one is more of a traditional series novel. It focuses more on the actual storyline, which is quite fortunately intriguing enough to pull you in and never let go.<br /><br />The world of the Witcher, most recently broadcasted by Netflix after having been stunningly presented in <i>The Witcher 3: Wild Hunt</i>, undoubtedly one of the most immersive and beautiful video games ever presented to the public, is shown just as enchantingly on the pages of the Witcher books, as they take the reader from the burning city of Cintra to the ancient Witcher fortress of Kaer Morhen and beyond.<br /><br />While it is still relatively unknown by comparison to the giants of the genre (as a result of coming from a non-English-speaking country), I would not hesitate to call this one of the most impressive series in fantasy. And with the rise in Witcher adaptations in recent years, it appears more and more people are finding their way to it.<br /><br /><b>Witcher reviews:</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792532185" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890591117" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793290591" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810132387" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of Contempt</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/866619209" rel="nofollow noopener">Baptism of Fire</a><br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200252982" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tower of the Swallow</a><br />#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200252988" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady of the Lake</a><br />#0 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404193589" rel="nofollow noopener">Season of Storms</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14773911870744341687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3133698215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3133698215" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3133698215?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575083189" href="/book/show/3804139-blood-of-elves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3133698215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13022627509196059093">Did I pick this up expressly because I saw the Netflix show and wanted more? Why yes, yes I am. Aka me and like 3898 other people are doing this (the reservations at my local library is hilariously long), but it actually makes me happy. TV show adaptions of books DO inspire people to go read the original source material! But I definitely enjoyed this more <i>because</i> I'd seen the show. I had all the actors in my heads for the characters and could totally imagine the humour and interactions. 😂Also th</span>
  <span id="freeText13022627509196059093" style="display:none">Did I pick this up expressly because I saw the Netflix show and wanted more? Why yes, yes I am. Aka me and like 3898 other people are doing this (the reservations at my local library is hilariously long), but it actually makes me happy. TV show adaptions of books DO inspire people to go read the original source material! But I definitely enjoyed this more <i>because</i> I'd seen the show. I had all the actors in my heads for the characters and could totally imagine the humour and interactions. 😂Also this basically picks up where the show left off. I assume S1 of the show is taken from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>, which I didn't know to read first!! So I read this one first!! Because it says book 1 but apparently really isn't!! Thx so much for that!!<br /><br />Also this fantasy is <i>old</i> but it made me so happy how inclusive it was? It was refreshingly (shockingly) not gross to women, it talked about menstruation for freaking once, and more pivotal female characters than men. Everyone turning to soft dough in the face of Ciri and the need to love and protect her was basically the best thing ever. Geralt is PUTTY IN HER HANDS. Also Ciri is this feral defiant child who wants to be a Witcher. Yennefer and Jaskier chat for a while and Jaskier legit goes "Oh I thought you only liked me as much as you like DEATH" because he still is an endearing pets. Yennefer and Geralt avoid each other because Unresolved Sexual Tension.<br /><br />I'm just sitting here, softly with mouth agape, realising adult fantasy CAN INDEED last a whole book without being monstrous offensive to women. (Wait, brb, need to go beat some other fantasy books over the head with this one.)<br /><br />The style was mostly dialogue; like maybe 70% of this book is pure dialogue. I would've liked more depth to the whole thing, the world and the characters particularly. And it didn't really have a typical plot arc. The ending was more like "leading up to the next episode" instead of rising to a climax and exploding into a finale. I feel like we fell into the ending? But I assume the climax encompasses the series as a whole. Which I INTEND TO FIND OUT. I SHALL READ MORE. So not my typical favourite style to read? But I did enjoy it.<br /><br /><b>So basically, if you love the Witcher on Netflix, do read this.</b> So much extra content and small quiet moments to laugh. As well as you learn more about the Witchers order. I know there's also a game, but my TBR just pterodactyl screamed at me. I shall go back to my books, my reading. 😌</span>
  <a data-text-id="13022627509196059093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1917549623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917549623" />
    <a title="Celise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653644-celise"><img alt="Celise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546382482p2/4653644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917549623?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celise" href="/user/show/4653644-celise">Celise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=fantasy-adult">fantasy-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917549623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10881438519326282385">For anyone who's played The Witcher games, or anyone who has not but is interested in dark fantasy, I encourage you to consider reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1128434.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___1_' title='The Last Wish (The Witcher, #1) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Wish</a>, which is the first of The Witcher books, an anthology of short stories. Read it before this, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18215192.Sword_of_Destiny__The_Witcher___2_' title='Sword of Destiny (The Witcher, #2) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sword of Destiny</a> too. They're good, and you'll thank yourself for it later when you're not trying to decipher the backstory behind this one. The Blood of Elves is the first full-length novel in the series, and I was not disappointed. It's even made it </span>
  <span id="freeText10881438519326282385" style="display:none">For anyone who's played The Witcher games, or anyone who has not but is interested in dark fantasy, I encourage you to consider reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1128434.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___1_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #1) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>, which is the first of The Witcher books, an anthology of short stories. Read it before this, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18215192.Sword_of_Destiny__The_Witcher___2_" title="Sword of Destiny (The Witcher, #2) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a> too. They're good, and you'll thank yourself for it later when you're not trying to decipher the backstory behind this one. The Blood of Elves is the first full-length novel in the series, and I was not disappointed. It's even made it onto my "favourites" shelf.<br /><br />The general concept is that Geralt, a Witcher created through elixirs and brutal mutilation as a child, hunts and kills monsters for pay. This volume is about the child Ciri, who we meet in the short stories of The Last Wish and The Sword of Destiny, and her training in both magic and witching (I don't know if that's what the Witcher craft is called but hey I used it). The other part of this is the brewing war between the Nilfgaardians and the countries on the other side of the river.<br /><br />Character relationships are complex and full of history. They're so tied together by destiny, yet so emotionally stunted towards each other that at some point it's just sad. Poetic and lovely, and not pathetic enough to become angsty and melodramatic. Ciri is kind of the light in the dark, probably to her detriment. She's the one to which Triss's longing for Geralt, and Yennefer's pain over him, is actually put into words. This is the first book in which Triss appears and while I was geared up to immediately feel bitterness towards her, none of Sapkowski's characters end up deserving that. All that said, this isn't a sappy romance love-fest, and is very much story-oriented.<br /><br />Sapkowski's sense of humour is exactly within my tastes too: cynical and quippy, as well as a little mean. Yennefer and Triss both have that sharp tongue that made me laugh out loud a few times, and Ciri is just comical by nature.<br /><br />And here's a less reviewy part and more of a collection of my thoughts. At this point, I'm not sure if Ciri being "destined" for Geralt means she's meant to eventually be his partner, or more of a daughter, and I have not played the games to know. Also no spoilers, please. Yennefer's initial resentment towards Ciri would be justified either way, either as a woman with a past with Geralt, or as a woman unable to bear her own children. In this volume at least, Ciri is his ward, and he trains her in Kaer Morhen to be a witcher. Her early training in magic (and how to survive puberty, let's be honest) is carried out by Triss Merigold, whom I adored for being one of the only characters who just said what they were feeling, and later by Yennefer. Yennefer's interactions with Ciri were my favourite part of the book, ultimately. In my opinion, Sapkowski writes the relationships between a young girl and her older female mentors with sincerity and impressive believability.<br /><br />I usually struggle with fantasy not making me truly feel things, but there's plenty of heart torture for me in these!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10881438519326282385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3191299874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17963241511963474342">Maybe I'm a slave to TV after all. I watched the Witcher production before picking up any of the short stories or the novels. Even before playing the games! (And I admit I still haven't played the games.)<br/><br/>So obviously, my opinion is going to be somewhat SKEWED from the rest of the hoards of fans of Sapkowski. Or maybe improved. Who knows?<br/><br/>The fact is... I had a wonderful time reading this. <br/><br/>At no point did I ever feel underwhelmed, think that the pacing was off, or want to complain about the lack o</span>
  <span id="freeText17963241511963474342" style="display:none">Maybe I'm a slave to TV after all. I watched the Witcher production before picking up any of the short stories or the novels. Even before playing the games! (And I admit I still haven't played the games.)<br /><br />So obviously, my opinion is going to be somewhat SKEWED from the rest of the hoards of fans of Sapkowski. Or maybe improved. Who knows?<br /><br />The fact is... I had a wonderful time reading this. <br /><br />At no point did I ever feel underwhelmed, think that the pacing was off, or want to complain about the lack of huge battles or epic whatnot. <br /><br />I knew this whole series was a character study first, a social commentary second, and a delightful worldbuilding/epic fantasy extravaganza third. And so, since I already loved the characters, I continued to love the characters, get awed about the full ramifications of the elves, the brewing war that would bring about much more than self-destruction, but the end of so much that was good in this flawed world, and was properly horrified by the other wars that had already happened. <br /><br />One could say that these novels are the effects and substance of massive amounts of Aftermath. And the TV show reflects that. We know things are all about to end. Spectacularly. And it is this over-story that keeps me at the table that is still, primarily, a delicious feast of characters.<br /><br />So I repeat. :) I loved this. I love them. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="17963241511963474342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1975978196" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1975978196" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1975978196?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=witcherverse">witcherverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1975978196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1492129074692715915">“Blood of Elves”, the third book in “The Witcher” series, is the first full length novel. I recommend reading the two short story collections first (“The Last Wish” and “The Sword of Destiny”) as they are linked together to form the background for this book. It will also give you a feel of the writing style and pacing of the whole series. This is not an action pack, high stakes thriller. This is a very slow, character driven tale where the enjoyment is taken from world-building escapism. I'm not</span>
  <span id="freeText1492129074692715915" style="display:none">“Blood of Elves”, the third book in “The Witcher” series, is the first full length novel. I recommend reading the two short story collections first (“The Last Wish” and “The Sword of Destiny”) as they are linked together to form the background for this book. It will also give you a feel of the writing style and pacing of the whole series. This is not an action pack, high stakes thriller. This is a very slow, character driven tale where the enjoyment is taken from world-building escapism. I'm not saying it's boring, but if you're use to modern western fantasy stories, you may not enjoy the slow pace. <br /><br />Though there is plenty of Geralt to go around, you’ll realize that this is really Ciri's story. It primarily offers some insight to her childhood after she's taken in by Geralt, showing the early relationships she had with the other characters. The backdrop, of course, is a distinctly sociopolitical tragedy. It mostly sets the scene of two enemy countries, on the brink of war, and how Geralt of Rivia is stuck in the middle, with both countries and numerous independent guilds after him and those he loves. I won't spoil anything but there's a scene that speaks loudly to the futility and toll of war: that very little is gained from killing in the end. <br /><br />Like the previous books, “Blood of Elves” is mostly based on dialogue -- using the characters words or thoughts to set the scene. This does, at times, make it feel a bit rushed and shallow but not enough to detract you from the story. The characters are memorable, the prose is far more sophisticated than in most fantasy, and the world Andrzej Sapkowski created is deeply compelling. I loved almost everything about it: from the sharp dialogue to the complex and multifaceted treatments of racism, sexism, colonialism and other socio-political issues that affect us in the real world. I particularly appreciated the way the book managed to operate simultaneously as serious fantasy and as a tongue-in-cheek deconstruction of the genre's tropes and cliches. <br /> <br />That, of course, is in part because the characters are just ridiculously good! I think Geralt is one of the most fully realized protagonists in fantasy. He's powerful, but reluctant to use his power in a way that might play into the world's terrible politics. He'd like nothing more than to opt-out completely and go about his business killing monsters for coin, but he can’t, and is inevitably dragged into affairs of war and peace. He's quiet, yet thoughtful; violent yet only hesitantly so; hard yet shows a greater capacity for empathy than anyone else in his world.<br />The powerful enchantresses he is romantically involved with, Yennefer of Vengerberg and Triss Merigold, are no less compelling. Any scene with Yennefer is pure gold! She's prideful, antagonistic and fierce. Yet, beneath the hard exterior -- undoubtedly caring and sympathetic--exactly the kind of complex, independent female character that male writers often have trouble writing. Her tortured relationship with Geralt is one for the ages, and works because she is his equal in every way. <br /> <br />“Blood of Elves” serves more as an introductory chapter to the overall story arc, and while it isn't the most exciting or plot driven story I've read -- it excels in delivering interesting, fleshed-out characters that you can't help but want to learn more about and sets the stage for the rest of the series. The ending is not an ending at all, but more of a lead into "A Time of Contempt”. Patience is required! If you ever want a more realistic approach to a fantasy world where politics of the realms have a larger impact on the world than a single character -- “The Witcher” is worth the effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1492129074692715915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3159379732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashwood (애쉬 우드)." href="/user/show/50173624-ashwood">Ashwood (애쉬 우드).</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3159379732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16212610488401741125"> “You’ve mistaken the stars reflected on the surface of the lake at night for the heavens.” <br/><br/> First off... I love this cover! It is absolutely stunning😍<br/><br/><br/> I started with Blood of Elves first, which was probably a mistake on my part, it feels like I should’ve started with the two short stories before this one, to really dive into the world of the Witcher. It was a really interesting journey, chapter-to-chapter, I never really knew what was going to happen next... whether the event was going to be bo</span>
  <span id="freeText16212610488401741125" style="display:none"> “You’ve mistaken the stars reflected on the surface of the lake at night for the heavens.” <br /><br /> First off... I love this cover! It is absolutely stunning😍<br /><br /><br /> I started with Blood of Elves first, which was probably a mistake on my part, it feels like I should’ve started with the two short stories before this one, to really dive into the world of the Witcher. It was a really interesting journey, chapter-to-chapter, I never really knew what was going to happen next... whether the event was going to be boring or super exciting (sometimes both in equal measure). <br /><br /><br /> The main characters absolutely fascinated me, the first and foremost, was Geralt all the way. Geralt was a bad-Aztec character, who was multi-faceted. He was a purebred warrior, with a heart of gold and even with all that he endured in his lifetime, he still had moments of compassion which was especially pronounced when Ciri was under his care. Not everyone liked him but the ones that did were the ones that counted.<br /> <br /> “I lose a great deal of my charm when one gets to know me better.” <br /><br /><br /> My second favorites were Ciri (duh, lol) and Yennefer. Those two complimented each other (not to say they always got along), from training, to friendship and even in conflict, they just really understood each other. They both gave a unique dimension to the story. <br /><br /> The one thing I had a bit of an issue with was the fact that they added sound effects at the moments that someone screamed or drew out a word longer than necessary to emphasize it (e.g. it went too slooowww) putting the word in italics would’ve sufficed. So instead of writing “she gave a sharp cry of desperation,” they had “ahhh,” in its place....Which would’ve probably have been helpful had I been listening to it in audiobook form but it added no bonus points for me while actually reading it. <br /><br /> As it stands now.. I enjoyed this book a fair amount but I’m not so crazy about the idea of diving into the rest of the books in the near future. <br /><br /> Favorite quote: <br /><br /> “The only thing which exists, which still counts, which still has any meaning.. is fear.”<br /> -Geralt, The Witcher</span>

<div id="review_1349512333" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1349512333" />
    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13459162-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579803798p2/13459162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1349512333?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/13459162-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1349512333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14736041058830219119"><b>Check out my review for Blood of Elves by Andrzej Sapkowski on Grimdark Magazine here: <a href='https://www.grimdarkmagazine.com/review-blood-of-elves-by-andrzej-sapkowski/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grimdark Magazine</a></b><br/><br/>Blood of Elves, the first ‘proper’ book in the tale of The Witcher, is a story of extreme training, bards songs and of course, swords. You’ll want to read this and the previous two instalments before you commence your journey into Netflix’s The Witcher. <br/><br/><b>“When you know about something it stops being a nightmare. When you know how to fight something, it stops being so threatening.”</b><br/><br/>The 3rd instal</span>
  <span id="freeText14736041058830219119" style="display:none"><b>Check out my review for Blood of Elves by Andrzej Sapkowski on Grimdark Magazine here: <a href="https://www.grimdarkmagazine.com/review-blood-of-elves-by-andrzej-sapkowski/" rel="nofollow noopener">Grimdark Magazine</a></b><br /><br />Blood of Elves, the first ‘proper’ book in the tale of The Witcher, is a story of extreme training, bards songs and of course, swords. You’ll want to read this and the previous two instalments before you commence your journey into Netflix’s The Witcher. <br /><br /><b>“When you know about something it stops being a nightmare. When you know how to fight something, it stops being so threatening.”</b><br /><br />The 3rd instalment into The Witcher moves away from the prior collections of short stories, and shifts into gear for the grand arc that is sure to come in the remaining 5 instalments. Where The Last Wish and Sword of Destiny focused on monster-slaying contracts, Blood of Elves has character development at the fore. It was my main gripe with the previous two stories, how there did not seem to be an over-arching scheme that would link everything together. <br /><br />I highly suggest that you begin your journey into the realm of The Witcher with The Last Wish, and then Sword of Destiny as they subtly introduce a vast range of characters. I was pleasantly surprised with the return of minor characters that had quirks and personality enough for me to distinctly remember them. <br /><br /><b>“To be neutral does not mean to be indifferent or insensitive. You don't have to kill your feelings. It's enough to kill hatred within yourself.”</b><br /><br />It is through Geralt’s interaction with other characters where the books come alive. The vast variety of dialogue sequences and subjects allows everyone to have their own voice, pardon the pun. Their voices and styles are distinct, if a lot of the time very wordy, which I will blame on the translation…maybe.<br /><br />If you’ve played the games, you’ll notice lots of references the makers made in honour of the books. Particular scenes, such as the training of a young ‘Witcher’. There is a surprise as Geralt is not the only POV. The most notable addition is Ciri’s side of things, which I wasn’t keen on at first (everyone always wants more Geralt,) but in the end really enjoyed it. She is a character that is growing on me and I am really looking forward to seeing where the story takes her.<br /><br /><b>“I know you’re almost forty, look almost thirty, think you’re just over twenty and act as though you’re barely ten.” </b><br /><br />The world building is solid, and gives the impression of a vast and well thought out world, from the Witcher haven of Kaer Morhen to the busy city of Novigrad. Characters that drift between places are met and so are characters that are key parts of regions. I’d have loved a map to go with the various names, which would have given me a real scope of the world, but I used my knowledge of the games (which is albeit probably slightly different to how Andrej Sapkowski imagined the world).<br /><br />I still managed to find the examples of a gender imbalance, which unfortunately I’ve come to expect from a Sapkowski book about the Witcher. Geralt is a good man, and someone who tries to treat everyone equally, but there were still instances in the general writing of it. Still, I was pleasantly surprised with Ciri’s POV and really enjoyed her portrayal.<br /><br />Now one thing I need to say is that I was desperate for more sword and sorcery. Geralt is one of the coolest guys and he has some really cool swords and I really wanted some cool swordplay and casting of signs and monster heads to go flying and… I could go on for a while. I would have enjoyed some more action. And some more classic fairy tale re-tellings. There was certainly enough talking in Blood of Elves, there could have been a few more instances of bloody fighting and some twists and turns. Hoping I’ll get my silver sword fix in the next instalment, Time of Contempt! <br /><br /><b>“Night and day the streets resounded with music, song, and the clinking of chalices and tankards, for it is well known that nothing is such thirsty work as the acquisition of knowledge.”</b><br /><br /><b>3/5 - Hoping for something better, but still enjoying what I received. This lukewarm dish is warming up and I have high hopes for the continuation of The Witcher Saga. The preparation for Netflix’s The Witcher is enjoyable, and I am sure will sweeten the TV show and Henry Cavill’s lovely wig. More swords next time, please! Igni!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14736041058830219119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73014378" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1843406376080387832">I "feel" (note the use of the word "feel" rather than "think") I should (have) like(ed) this book better. The plot sounds very interesting. The girl Ciri, child of promise and prophecy (yes a common motif in fantasy and folklore) who was promised to the Witcher before she was born. (Evil faeries and so on used to claim that promise). The story of her "education", training, change and all the people around who want to protect or use her. <br/><br/>But I just found the book a sort of yawner. It opens with a</span>
  <span id="freeText1843406376080387832" style="display:none">I "feel" (note the use of the word "feel" rather than "think") I should (have) like(ed) this book better. The plot sounds very interesting. The girl Ciri, child of promise and prophecy (yes a common motif in fantasy and folklore) who was promised to the Witcher before she was born. (Evil faeries and so on used to claim that promise). The story of her "education", training, change and all the people around who want to protect or use her. <br /><br />But I just found the book a sort of yawner. It opens with a really "grab ya" scene of an attack on a city that turns out to be a partial and suppressed memory of Cir coming out in a dream... and jumps to a bard singing about "someone" or "some people" that all the listeners "just know" are Ciri, Geralt etc. But it rolls on so slowly.<br /><br />The races here a a little different than we find elsewhere but not greatly. The magic folk, druids, priests who populate the book never grab me and I just couldn't get into the story. I found myself skimming the book going from Triss' memories to Ciri's training, from events to visions and all along I was just losing interest.<br /><br />Maybe it's me and my own taste. I see a lot of people like this book and I'm certainly glad you found a volume you like. I liked the first book or prequel to this one (The Last Wish) pretty well, but this one just never drew me in. I really don't care for it all that much.<br /><br />I do apologize to you who like this book greatly, as I've noted many times it's simple a matter of taste. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1843406376080387832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12825892171916534477">4.5 stars<br/><br/>I believe I did a bad decision when I started the series with The Last Wish. May be I have to read the novels after I read all the main books. Long story short: I picked The Last Wish after I hear Daniel Greene ( <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jAfWFDxqIO8' rel='nofollow noopener'>my link text</a> )on you tube that he is reading The Witcher and is so good I have to try, but I did not like the book.   <span id="freeText12825892171916534477" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />I believe I did a bad decision when I started the series with The Last Wish. May be I have to read the novels after I read all the main books. I believe I did a bad decision when I started the series with The Last Wish. May be I have to read the novels after I read all the main books. Long story short: I picked The Last Wish after I hear Daniel Greene ( <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jAfWFDxqIO8" rel="nofollow noopener">my link text</a> )on you tube that he is reading The Witcher and is so good I have to try, but I did not like the book. Most of the time we have similar tastes and exactly the things I find annoying in a book, he also highlights them, so it surprised me a little that the book didn't captivate me. After Cavil got the role of Geralt I have to see the tv show, so in my characteristic style I cannot see a movie if it is made after a book until I read the book, and here I am!<br /><br />Blood of Elves I like it a lot. I really loved the characterization. Both in our main characters Geralt of Rivia and Ciri, and all their supporting characters. The dynamics of relationships between characters in this book are complex and full of history. brought together by destiny, but emotionally stunted towards each other. Geralt, Yennefer, Triss, and Ciri all have emotions that will captivate your heart and you will root for them in different ways. What I love about Yennefer and Triss is that they have both a sharp tongue, that "woman in control" attitude I like to see more in feminine characters. <br />This book has a perfect balance between action, dialogue and description, and when conversation take over, is so well written that does not fill pages just for the sake of making the book thicker, but simply provides information for the reader to understand this world. It was a struggle for me and a little confusing because of the similar names, and when it’s not entirely made clear who it talking .<br /><br />So, overall, I really really enjoyed the read and want to certainly continue the series.</span>
